‡§â‡§™‡§≠‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç, ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§, ‡§π‡•á ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ! ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‚Äò‡§§‡•á’ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•å ‘‡§π‡§∞‡•Ä’ ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡•å ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‘‡§®‡•Å’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‘‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ã‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§

‡§∏‡•Å‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‘‡§Æ‡§ò‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç’ ! ‡§Ü‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ! ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•Å-‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‘‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ’ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‘‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø’ ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡•§ “‡§µ‡§¶‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§É”- (‡§ß‡§æ. ‡§™‡§æ. ‡§≠‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§Ü. ‡•ß‡•ß) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É-‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‘‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§É’ ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡•Ä‡§°‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É, ‘‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§É’ ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‘‡§µ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å’ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø’ ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø, ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•©‡•Æ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. They stand by the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya fire (worshipping) with two (verses) addressed to Indra [viz. Rig-veda I, 82, 2-3; VƒÅj. S. III, 51-52], since the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya is Indra. ‘The friends have eaten, and regaled themselves, and have shaken off (the enemies) 69; the self-shining bards have extolled (thee) with their newest hymn: yoke, then, thy pair of bay steeds, O Indra!–To thee, the splendid, we will sing praises, O bountiful one! Thus praised, do thou now issue forth, with well-filled car, agreeably to our desire! yoke, then, thy pair of bay steeds, O Indra!’

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••
‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡•§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ö ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É‡•• ‡§Ü·≥ò ‡§® ‡§è‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§¶·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ·≥ò‡§∏‡•á‡•• ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á‡•• ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ã ‡§¶·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú·≥ò‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§è‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§®·≥ò‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§·≥´‡§Ç·≥≠‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å·≥ò‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••
‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ö ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§Ü·≥ò ‡§® ‡§è‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§¶·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ·≥ò‡§∏‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Ç·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ã ‡§¶·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§§·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§è‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§®·≥ò‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§§·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ “‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡•§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡•• ‡§Ü ‡§® ‡§è‡§§‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∏‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç ‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡•• ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å ‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•´‡•©-‡•´‡•´) ‡•§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§É- ‡§§‡§¶‡•Å ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π- ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•©‡•Ø ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø 70 ‡•§ ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø-‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø’ ‡§Ü‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•á “‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á-” ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É- ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‘‡§Æ‡§®‡§É’ ‘‡§®‡•Å’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ü‡§π‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á’ ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡•á‡§® ? ‘‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡•á‡§®’ ‡§®‡§∞‡•à‡§É ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£, ‘‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç’ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‘‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É’ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§®‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡••

‡§Ü ‡§® ‡§è‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‘‡§Æ‡§®‡§É’ ‘‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‘‡§è‡§§‡•Å’ ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•Å ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ? ‘‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•á, ‘‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø’ ‡§¨‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø, ‘‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∏‡•á’ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø, ‘‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç’ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‘‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö’ ‘‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á’ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ “‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ö”- (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•ß) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡••

‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‘‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§É !’ ‘‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä ‘‡§ú‡§®‡§É’ ‘‡§®‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‘‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‚Äô ‡•§ ‚Äò‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç’ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‘‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç’ ‡§ó‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§∏‡§ö‡•á‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•á ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π- ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§®’ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‘‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§É,’ ‡§Ö‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‚Äú‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç-‚Äù ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‚Äò‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡•å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á’ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø, ‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡•©‡•Ø ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon they return to the GƒÅrhapatya and stand by it worshipping with the verses (Rig-veda X, 57,3-5; VƒÅj. S. III, 53-55), ‘We invoke the Mind with man-lauding strain 71, and with the hymns of the fathers.–May the Mind come back to us for (us to obtain) wisdom, vigour, and life, and that we may long see the sun!–May the divine race restore to us the Mind, O Fathers, that we may abide with the living kind!’ They have indeed been performing the sacrifice to the Manes; but now they return to the (land of the) living: hence he says, ‘That we may abide with the living kind!’

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò ‡§≠‡•Ç·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§·≥ò‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò ‡§≠‡•Ç‡•ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§·≥ò‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ, ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§™‡§§‡§ø- “‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡§§”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•® ‡•§ ‡•©‡•ß) ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡•• ‡•™‡•¶ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§ú‡§™‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞ 70 ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§•’ ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‘‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡§É’ ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§Ç ‘‡§¶‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§ø,’ ‘‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É’ ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•Ä’ ‘‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ,’ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø “‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É, ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡•™‡•¶ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he who has presented (the obsequial cakes) again shifts his sacrificial cord to the right shoulder and betakes. himself (to the fire in the shed), and mutters (VƒÅj. S. II, 31), ‘The

Fathers have regaled themselves: like bulls they came each to his share:’ whereby he means to say, ’they have eaten each his own share.’

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§π‡§æ·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡••

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡••
‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§·≥ò‡§∞‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Æ·≥ò‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ·≥ò‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å·≥ò‡§∑‡•á ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•á·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò ‡§® ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ï·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡§Ç·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§™·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø, ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø- ‚Äú‡§Ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‚Äù ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‚Äú‡§Ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ" ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ” ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡•ç- ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§® ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§§‡•à’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç- ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•™‡•ß ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§ï‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ú‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡•á’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§®‡•á‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§ï‡§•‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç (‡§∂. ‡§™. ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç. ‡•® ‡•§ ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•® ‡•§ ‡•®‡•©) ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø ‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∏‡§≤‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§Æ ‘‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç’ ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø ‘‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ’ ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§§‡•à’ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§á‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§≤‡§µ‡§ø’ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∏‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•™‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He now takes the vessel of water and again, while sprinkling, walks thrice round (the altar) from left to right (sunwise). With ‘N.N., wash thyself!’ he pours out water (in the respective corner) for the Sacrificer’s father to wash himself; with ‘N.N., wash thyself!’ for the grandfather; with ‘N.N., wash thyself!’ for the great-grandfather. As one would pour out water for (a guest) who has taken food with him, so in this case. And as to his again walking thrice round from left to right, while sprinkling,–they think, ‘This holy work of ours shall be accomplished sunwise 72,’ and hence he walks thrice round from left to right, while sprinkling.

Eggeling
  1. He then pulls down the tuck (of the nether garment) 74 and makes obeisance (to the Fathers). The tuck, doubtless, is sacred to the Fathers: hence he makes obeisance to them after pulling down the tuck; and obeisance means worship: hence he thereby recognises them as entitled to worship. Six times he makes obeisance to them, since there are six seasons, and the Fathers are the seasons: hence he thereby establishes his sacrifice in the seasons,–that is why he makes obeisance six times 75. ‘Give houses

unto us; O Fathers!’ he (further) says, because the Fathers are the guardians of houses;–and this is the prayer for blessing at this sacred performance.

Eggeling
  1. He (the Adhvaryu) then says, ‘Brahman, I shall step forward.’ Thereupon he puts the stick (reserved at the time of kindling) on (the fire), and says, ‘Agnƒ´dh, trim the fire!’ He then takes the two spoons and crosses over to the west side. After crossing over and calling for the ‘≈örausha·π≠,’ he says (to the HotrÃ•), ‘Pronounce the offering-prayer to the gods!’ He performs two after-offerings, omitting the one to the Barhis; for the Barhis means offspring: hence he performs two after-offerings, omitting the one to the Barhis, lest he should consign his offspring to the Fathers.

Eggeling
  1. He (the ƒÄgnƒ´dhra) then says, ‘Discourse together!’ [The Adhvaryu asks], ‘Has he gone (to the gods), Agnƒ´dh?’–‘He has gone!’–‘Bid (the gods) hear!’–‘May one (or, they) hear!’–‘Goodspeed to the divine HotrÃ•s! Success to the human!–Pronounce the All-hail and blessing!’ Thus saying, he merely touches the enclosing-sticks, but does not (now) throw them (into the fire). The Barhis and enclosing-sticks he throws in afterwards 81.

Eggeling
  1. And here some throw also the remaining sacrificial food into the fire; but let him not do so; for that (remaining havis) is the residue of an offering; and lest he should offer the residue of an offering, let them (the priests) rather throw it into the water or eat it.

The KƒÅ·πáva MS. has as follows: Thereupon, by way of i·∏çƒÅ, they place that same porridge into the hand of the HotrÃ•. The HotrÃ•, having invoked it, smells it. They hand it to the ƒÄgnƒ´dhra.   62. 432:1 See II, 4, 2, 16 seq. According to the comm. on KƒÅty. V, q, 27, some sprinkle three times round the altar for each of the three ancestors. But according to the Paddhati, he sprinkles once round the altar, beginning from the north-west corner; then he sits down and pours out water in that corner for the father. Thereupon, after walking round in the opposite direction (from left to right) to the south-west corner, he again sprinkles all round, and in the same way pours out water in that corner for the grandfather; and after retracing his steps as far as the south-east corner, he performs the same circumambulation, and pours out water in that corner for the great-grandfather; whereupon he again retraces his steps up to the west of the altar. ↩︎

  63. 432:2 In the case of a sacrificer whose father is still alive, these ceremonies are performed in honour of the father’s father, grandfather, and great-grandfather. ↩︎
